Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
beginner
4 min
Abu Sa'd's Visits to Baghdad and Teachers
Al-Khatib al-Baghdadi's report on Abu Sa'd's travels and teachers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will know that Abu Sa'd visited Baghdad multiple times, his last visit during the lifetime of al-Daraqutni, and his narration from key teachers.

Core Idea
He was a traveler in pursuit of knowledge, and his last visit to Baghdad was in the time of the great hadith scholar al-Daraqutni.

The biography concludes with an additional report from the famous historian al-Khatib al-Baghdadi, confirming that Abu Sa'd visited Baghdad several times and studied under notable scholars. This lesson provides further context on his scholarly network.

Guided Path
1
Read the report
Read the passage which includes the chain of transmission from al-Khatib.
Notice the chain: al-Ghassani and al-Muqri' from al-Khatib.
2
Identify key points
Note that he visited Baghdad more than once and his last visit was during al-Daraqutni's lifetime.
Al-Daraqutni was a prominent hadith scholar.
3
List the teachers mentioned
The passage mentions he narrated from his father, al-Asamm, and others.
The text cuts off mid-list.

الجرجان قال أنا أبو القسم حمزة بن يوسف بن إبراهيم السهمي في كتاب تاريخ جرجان قال إسماعيل بن أحمد بن إبراهيم بن إسماعيل بن العباس أبو سعد الإسماعيلى كان أمام زمانه مقدما في الفقه وأصول الفقه والعربية رحمة الله عليه ورضوانه حججت معه سنة أربع وثمانين حيث رجع من نصف البادية وحج في سنة خمس وثمانين إلى أن رجع إلى وطنه كنت معه لم أره تغير عن خلقه النفس كان معظما مبجلا في جميع البلدان روى عن أبي بكر محمد بن إبراهيم الشافعي ومحمد بن أسحق الفاكهى ودعلج وعن الأصم محمد بن يعقوب حديثاً واحداً وعن عبد الله ابن عدى كتاب الضعفاء وجمعه مسند مالك بن أنس توفى ليلة الجمعة النصف من شهر ربيع الآخر سنة ست وتسعين وثلاثمائة وصلى عليه أخوه أبو نصر الإسماعيلى فى صحراء باب الخندق فى جمع عظيم لم أر مثل ذلك الجمع بجرجان في تشييع جنازة أحد قط ودفن عند رأس والده أبى بكر الإسماعيلي توفى وهو ابن ثلاث وستين سنة ومما أكرمه الله به ورفع قدره به أنه مات وهو في صلاة المغرب يقرأ إياك نعبد وإياك نستعين ففاضت نفسه ومما أكرمه الله به أنه حين قربت وفاته ذهب منه ما كان يملكه من المال والضياع وكان يوجه القطن إلى باب الأبواب جميع فغرق الجميع في البحر وكانت له بضاعة تحمل من أصبهان فوقع عليها الأكراد فأخذوها وكان يحمل له من خراسان شئ من الحنطة فوقع عليه قوم وأغاروا عليه وكان له ضيعة بقرية تعرف بكوشكى أمر قابوس بن وشمكير أن يقلع أشجارها فقلع جميع ذلك وكبست القناة وقبض جميع ضياعه وخلف من الأولاد أبا معمر المفضل وأبا العلاء السرى وأبا سعيد سعد وأبا الفضل مسعدة وأبا الحسن مبشر وابنتين فأما أبو معمر فصار أماماً مقدماً في العلوم وأبو العلاء فإنه أيضاً صار عالماً في الفقه والأدب حضرت يوما مجلس الإمام أبي بكر الإسماعيلي على باب داره ننتظر خروجه فخرج الإمام أبو بكر أحمد بن إبراهيم الإسماعيلي وهو مستبشر وبيده جزء فجلس وقال أنشدنى ابنى أبو سعد وأنشدنا ثم أنشدنا الإمام أبو سعد بعد ما أنشدنا والده عنه أنى أدخرت ليوم ورد منیتی عند الإله من الأمور خطيرا وهو اليقين بأنه الأحد الذي مازلت منه بفضله مغمورا وشهادتي أن النبي محمدا كان الرسول مبشراً ونذيرا وبراءتي من كل شرك قاله من لا يقر بفعله مبرورا ومحبتي آل النبي وصحبه كلا أراه بالجميل جديرا وتمسكى بالشافعي وعلمه ذاك الذي فتق العلوم بحورا وجميل ظني بالاله لما جنت نفسى وأن حرمت على شرورا أن الظلوم لنفسه إن يأته مستغفراً يجد الآله غفورا فاشهد الهي أننى مستغفر لا أستطيع لما مننت شكوراً هذا الذى أعددته لشدائدي وكفى بربی هاديا ونصيرا أخبرنا الشيخ أبو الحسن على بن أحمد بن منصور الغساني وأبو منصور محمد بن عبد الملك المقرى قالا قال لنا الشيخ الإمام أبو بكر أحمد ابن على بن ثابت الخطيب إسماعيل بن أحمد بن إبراهيم بن إسماعيل ابن العباس أبو سعد الجرجاني المعروف بالإسماعيلى ورد بغداد غير مرة وآخر وروده كان في حياة أبي الحسن الدارقطني وحدث عن أبيه أبي بكر الإسماعيلي وعن أبي العباس الأصم النيسابورى ومحمد بن أحمد ابن
He mentioned some of the second stratum, who are the companions of his companions, those who followed his path in principles and were disciplined by his manners. Among them is Abu Sa'd ibn Abi Bakr al-Isma'ili al-Jurjani, may God have mercy on him. Abu al-Qasim ibn Abi Bakr al-Dallal informed us, saying: Abu al-Qasim ibn Abi al-Fadl al-Jurjani informed us, saying: Abu al-Qasim Hamza ibn Yusuf ibn Ibrahim al-Sahmi informed us in the book 'History of Jurjan', saying: Isma'il ibn Ahmad ibn Ibrahim ibn Isma'il ibn al-Abbas Abu Sa'd al-Isma'ili was the imam of his time, foremost in jurisprudence, principles of jurisprudence, Arabic language, writing, conditions, and theology. He authored a large book on principles of jurisprudence called 'Tahdhib al-Nazar', and he has a book on beverages refuting al-Jassas. He taught jurisprudence for many years, and a group of jurists from Jurjan, Tabaristan, and other regions graduated under him. He possessed praiseworthy qualities that cannot be counted: deep piety, striving in worship and knowledge, concern for religious affairs, sincerity to Islam, good character, cheerfulness, generosity in feeding others, and spending wealth—I cannot enumerate it all. May God's mercy and pleasure be upon him. I performed Hajj with him in the year 384, when he returned from halfway through the desert, and he performed Hajj in 385 until he returned to his homeland. I was with him; I never saw him change from his noble character. He was honored and revered in all countries. He narrated from Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Ibrahim al-Shafi'i, Muhammad ibn Ishaq al-Fakihi, Da'laj, and from al-Asamm Muhammad ibn Ya'qub one hadith, and from Abdullah ibn Adi the book 'al-Du'afa', and he collected the Musnad of Malik ibn Anas. He died on the night of Friday, the middle of Rabi' al-Akhir, in the year 396. His brother Abu Nasr al-Isma'ili prayed over him in the desert of Bab al-Khandaq in a huge crowd—I never saw such a crowd in Jurjan for anyone's funeral procession. He was buried at the head of his father Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili. He died at the age of sixty-three. Among the honors God bestowed upon him and elevated his rank thereby was that he died while performing the Maghrib prayer reciting 'You alone we worship, and You alone we ask for help', and his soul departed. And among the honors God bestowed upon him was that when his death approached, the wealth and estates he owned left him. He used to send cotton to Bab al-Abwab, and all of it sank in the sea. He had merchandise carried from Isfahan, and Kurds attacked and took it. He had some wheat brought from Khurasan, and a group attacked and looted it. He had an estate in a village known as Kushki; Qabus ibn Wushmagir ordered its trees to be uprooted, so all that was uprooted, the canal was blocked, and all his estates were seized. He left behind from his children: Abu Mu'mar al-Mufaddal, Abu al-'Ala' al-Sari, Abu Sa'id Sa'd, Abu al-Fadl Mas'ada, Abu al-Hasan Mubashshir, and two daughters. As for Abu Mu'mar, he became an imam foremost in the sciences; and Abu al-'Ala', he also became a scholar in jurisprudence and literature. One day I attended the gathering of Imam Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili at the door of his house, waiting for his exit. Then Imam Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ibrahim al-Isma'ili came out, beaming, with a volume in his hand. He sat down and said: 'My son Abu Sa'd recited to me,' and he recited to us. Then Imam Abu Sa'd recited to us after his father had recited to us from him: 'I have stored up for the day of my death a serious matter with God: it is certainty that He is the One, with whose favor I have always been overwhelmed; and my testimony that Muhammad is the Prophet, a bringer of good news and a warner; and my disassociation from every polytheism uttered by one who does not acknowledge His action, approved; and my love for the family of the Prophet and his Companions, all of them I see as worthy of good; and my adherence to al-Shafi'i and his knowledge—that is he who split open the seas of knowledge; and my good opinion of God, even though my soul has committed evil and [even though] I am deprived of evils; that the one who is unjust to himself, if he comes to Him seeking forgiveness, he finds God forgiving. So bear witness, my God, that I am seeking forgiveness—I cannot be sufficiently grateful for what You have bestowed. This is what I have prepared for my hardships—sufficient is my Lord as a Guide and Helper.' The shaykh Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Ahmad ibn Mansur al-Ghassani and Abu Mansur Muhammad ibn Abd al-Malik al-Muqri' informed us, both saying: The shaykh Imam Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ali ibn Thabit al-Khatib said to us: Isma'il ibn Ahmad ibn Ibrahim ibn Isma'il ibn al-Abbas Abu Sa'd al-Jurjani, known as al-Isma'ili, visited Baghdad more than once, and his last visit was during the lifetime of Abu al-Hasan al-Daraqutni. He narrated from his father Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili, from Abu al-Abbas al-Asamm al-Naysaburi, and from Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn...
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry about Abu Sa'd al-Isma'ili (d. 396 AH). It begins by placing him among the second stratum of scholars who followed the path of the author's teacher. The passage then details his full name, his status as an imam, his expertise in numerous fields including jurisprudence, principles of jurisprudence, Arabic, writing, conditions, and theology. He authored a major work on usul al-fiqh called 'Tahdhib al-Nazar' and a refutation of al-Jassas on beverages. He taught for many years and many students graduated from him. The author then lists his praiseworthy qualities: deep piety, striving, good character, generosity, etc. The author mentions that he performed Hajj with him twice and observed his consistent noble character. Next, the passage lists his teachers and narrations: from al-Shafi'i, al-Fakihi, Da'laj, al-Asamm, and Ibn 'Adi, and he collected Malik's Musnad. Then the death: on a Friday night in Rabi' al-Akhir 396, at age 63, prayed over by his brother, buried near his father. A notable honor: he died while reciting 'Iyyaka na'budu wa iyyaka nasta'in' in Maghrib prayer. Additionally, before his death, all his wealth and properties were taken from him through a series of misfortunes: cotton lost at sea, merchandise taken by Kurds, wheat looted, and an estate ordered destroyed by Qabus ibn Wushmagir. This was a sign of honor, as he left the world detached. He left several children, among whom two became scholars. The passage then includes a poem composed by Abu Sa'd, which he recited to his father and then to the author. The poem expresses his preparation for death: certainty in God's oneness, testimony of prophethood, disassociation from shirk, love for the Prophet's family and Companions, adherence to al-Shafi'i, and hope in God's forgiveness. The final part is a report from al-Khatib al-Baghdadi confirming that al-Isma'ili visited Baghdad multiple times, with his last visit during the lifetime of al-Daraqutni, and that he narrated from his father and al-Asamm. The text cuts off mid-chain likely continuing to list more teachers.

Key Takeaway
Abu Sa'd al-Isma'ili was a traveling scholar who visited Baghdad multiple times and narrated from notable teachers including al-Daraqutni.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever traveled far to seek sacred knowledge, or have you only taken what was convenient? What does Abu Sa'd's multiple visits to Baghdad teach you about the effort required to learn from great scholars?
?
The last visit of Abu Sa'd coincided with the lifetime of al-Daraqutni—a deliberate pursuit. Who are the scholars of our time you are intentionally seeking out? If none, what is holding you back?
?
Abu Sa'd learned from his father and many other teachers. Are you limiting yourself to one source of knowledge? How can you expand your learning network to gain a more comprehensive understanding of your faith?

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
beginner
5 min
Biography of Abu Sa'd al-Isma'ili
Ibn Asakir records the biography of Abu Sa'd al-Isma'ili with multiple chains of transmission.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly profile, travels, teachers, students, and virtues of Abu Sa'd al-Isma'ili as recorded by Ibn 'Asakir.

Core Idea
Abu Sa'd al-Isma'ili was a distinguished Shafi'i jurist and leader in Jurjan.

Ibn 'Asakir presents the biography of Abu Sa'd al-Isma'ili through multiple chains of transmission, each adding details about his lineage, travels, teachers, students, death, and praise. This passage highlights his scholarly credentials and his esteemed position in Jurjan.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the full Arabic passage and its translation to get a sense of the biographical content. Notice the multiple chains of transmission.
The passage begins with a chain from al-Khatib al-Baghdadi.
2
Identify the three reports
The biography is composed of three main reports. Distinguish each: the first from al-Khatib, the second from al-Shirazi, and the third from al-Ghassani. Note what each report contributes.
Each report ends with a death date or additional praise.
3
Examine the teachers and students
List the teachers mentioned (e.g., his father Abu Bakr, al-Asamm, etc.) and the students (e.g., al-Ruyani, al-Khallal). Reflect on the scholarly network.
He studied under his own father, showing a family tradition.
4
Analyze the praise from al-Sahib ibn Abbad
Read the poetic praise describing Abu Sa'd's teaching and virtues. Consider how such eulogies elevated his status.
The praise compares him to a ‘scholar son of a scholar’.
5
Confirm the death date
Note that two reports confirm the death year 396 AH, one specifying the month of Rabi' al-Akhir. This shows careful historical recording.
The multiple reports ensure accuracy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أخبرنا الشيخ أبو الحسن على بن أحمد بن منصور الغساني وأبو منصور محمد بن عبد الملك المقرى قالا قال لنا الشيخ الإمام أبو بكر أحمد ابن على بن ثابت الخطيب : إسماعيل بن أحمد بن إبراهيم بن إسماعيل ابن العباس أبو سعد الجرجاني المعروف بالإسماعيلى ورد بغداد غير مرة وآخر وروده كان في حياة أبي الحسن الدارقطني ، وحدث عن أبيه أبي بكر الإسماعيلي وعن أبي العباس الأصم النيسابورى ومحمد بن أحمد ابن جعفر الدينوري ومحمد بن علی بن دحيم الكوفي وعبد الله بن عدی الجرجاني حدثنا عنه محمد بن أحمد بن شعيب الروياني وأبو محمد الخلال وعلى بن الحسن التنوخي وكان ثقة فاضلا فقيها على مذهب الشافعي وكان سخيًا جواداً مفضلاً على أهل العلم والرياسة بجرجان إلى اليوم في ولده وأهل بيته . أخبرنا الشيخ أبو القسم إسماعيل بن السمرقندى قال ثنا الشيخ الإمام أبو إسحق إبراهيم ابن علی بن یوسف الشيرازي قال أبو سعد إسماعيل بن أحمد بن إبراهيم بن إسماعيل بن العباس الإسماعيلي مات سنة ست وتسعين وثلاثمائة وجمع بين رياسة الدين والدنيا بجرجان وكان فقيهاً أديباً جواداً أخذ العلم عن أبيه أبي بكر الإسماعيلى وفيه وفى أخيه أبي نصر وأبيهما أبى بكر يقول الصاحب بن عباد في رسالته : وأما الفقيه أبو نصر فإذا جاء حدثنا وأخبرنا فصادع وصادق ونافذ وناطق وأما أنت أيها الفقيه أبا سعد فمن يراك كيف تدرس وتفتى وتحاضر وتروى وتكتب وتملى علم أنك الحبر بن الحبر والبحر ابن البحر والضياء بن الفجر وأبو سعد بن أبي بكر بن نجم الله شيخكم الأكبر فإن الثناء عليه غنم والنساء بمثله عقم فليفخر به أهل جرجان ما سال واديها وأذن مناديها أخبرنا الشيخ أبو الحسن بن أبي العباس الغساني قال ثنا أحمد بن على البغدادي قال حدثني أبو سعد إسماعيل بن على بن الحسن الواعظ الأستراباذي قال توفى أبو سعد الإسماعيلي بجرجان في شهر ربيع الآخر من سنة ست وتسعين وثلاثمائة
The Shaykh Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Ahmad ibn Mansur al-Ghassani and Abu Mansur Muhammad ibn Abd al-Malik al-Maqri' informed us, both saying: The Imam Shaykh Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ali ibn Thabit al-Khatib said to us: Isma'il ibn Ahmad ibn Ibrahim ibn Isma'il ibn al-Abbas Abu Sa'd al-Jurjani, known as al-Isma'ili, visited Baghdad more than once, and his last visit was during the lifetime of Abu al-Hasan al-Daraqutni. He narrated from his father Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili, and from Abu al-Abbas al-Asamm al-Naysaburi, Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Ja'far al-Dinawari, Muhammad ibn Ali ibn Dahaym al-Kufi, and Abd Allah ibn Adi al-Jurjani. Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Shu'ayb al-Ruyani, Abu Muhammad al-Khallal, and Ali ibn al-Hasan al-Tanukhi narrated from him. He was trustworthy, virtuous, a jurist according to the school of al-Shafi'i, and was generous, munificent, and favored the people of knowledge and leadership in Jurjan to this day among his children and household. The Shaykh Abu al-Qasim Isma'il ibn al-Samarqandi informed us, saying: The Imam Shaykh Abu Ishaq Ibrahim ibn Ali ibn Yusuf al-Shirazi narrated to us, saying: Abu Sa'd Isma'il ibn Ahmad ibn Ibrahim ibn Isma'il ibn al-Abbas al-Isma'ili died in the year 396 AH. He combined religious and worldly leadership in Jurjan, and was a jurist, literary man, and generous. He acquired knowledge from his father Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili. Concerning him, his brother Abu Nasr, and their father Abu Bakr, al-Sahib ibn Abbad said in his epistle: 'As for the jurist Abu Nasr, when he comes narrating and informing, he is a speaker, truthful, penetrating, and articulate. As for you, O jurist Abu Sa'd, whoever sees you in how you teach, give fatwas, lecture, narrate, write, and dictate knows that you are a scholar son of a scholar, a sea son of a sea, a radiance son of a dawn. And Abu Sa'd ibn Abi Bakr ibn Najm Allah, your greatest shaykh, for praise of him is gain and women are barren of the like of him. So let the people of Jurjan boast of him as long as its valley flows and its caller calls.' The Shaykh Abu al-Hasan ibn Abi al-Abbas al-Ghassani informed us, saying: Ahmad ibn Ali al-Baghdadi narrated to us, saying: Abu Sa'd Isma'il ibn Ali ibn al-Hasan al-Wa'iz al-Astarabadi narrated to me, saying: Abu Sa'd al-Isma'ili died in Jurjan in the month of Rabi' al-Akhir of the year 396 AH.
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry for Abu Sa'd al-Isma'ili (d. 396 AH), a prominent scholar from Jurjan. The biography is structured through multiple chains of transmission, each providing different details. The first report, from al-Khatib al-Baghdadi, gives his full name and lineage, noting his multiple visits to Baghdad, his last visit during the lifetime of al-Daraqutni. It lists his teachers, including his own father Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili, and his students. It then praises him as trustworthy, virtuous, a Shafi'i jurist, generous, and favoring scholars. The second report, from al-Shirazi, states his death year (396 AH) and adds that he combined religious and worldly leadership in Jurjan, being a jurist, literary man, and generous. It then quotes a lengthy praise from al-Sahib ibn Abbad, which extols both Abu Sa'd and his brother Abu Nasr, highlighting Abu Sa'd's teaching, fatwa-giving, lecturing, and dictating, and calling him a 'scholar son of a scholar.' The third report, from al-Ghassani, confirms the death date more precisely in the month of Rabi' al-Akhir of 396 AH. The biography thus establishes Abu Sa'd's scholarly credentials, his character, and his status in Jurjan.

Key Terms
أبو سعد الإسماعيلي
أبو بكر الإسماعيلي
الشافعي
جرجان
الصاحب بن عباد
وفاة 396 هـ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Abu Sa'd al-Isma'ili is the same as his father Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili.
Correction: Abu Sa'd is the son of Abu Bakr, distinguished by his own name and biography.

Checkpoint
When did Abu Sa'd al-Isma'ili die according to the passage?
A) 386 AH
B) 396 AH
C) 406 AH
D) 376 AH

Key Takeaway
Abu Sa'd al-Isma'ili (d. 396 AH) was a prominent Shafi'i jurist, generous benefactor, and a leading scholar in Jurjan, as attested by multiple authorities.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage says Abu Sa'd combined religious and worldly leadership. In your own life, are you striving to excel in both your spiritual and worldly responsibilities? What is one specific change you can make this week to better integrate your deen and dunya?
?
You see Abu Sa'd's generosity towards scholars and students. Reflect on your own use of wealth and position: are you prioritising the support of knowledge and people of knowledge? What is one concrete step you can take to become more generous in this area?
?
The praise from al-Sahib ibn Abbad highlights Abu Sa'd's teaching, writing, and dictating. How seriously do you take the task of transmitting knowledge? Is there a piece of knowledge you've learned that you could teach or share with others today? Write down one specific action you will take this week.

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
beginner
4 min
Abu Sa'd al-Isma'ili: A Scholar of Jurjan
Ibn Asakir transmits the biography of Abu Sa'd al-Isma'ili, noting his scholarship and generosity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the life and scholarly legacy of Abu Sa'd al-Isma'ili as recorded by Ibn 'Asakir, including his combination of religious and worldly leadership and the high praise he received from al-Sahib ibn 'Abbad.

Core Idea
Abu Sa'd al-Isma'ili embodied the ideal of combining religious scholarship with worldly leadership.

This passage from Tabyin Kadhib al-Muftari presents Ibn 'Asakir's biographical entry for the distinguished scholar Abu Sa'd al-Isma'ili. Through a chain of transmission and a poetic encomium from the famous vizier al-Sahib ibn 'Abbad, we learn about his death, his combined leadership in religion and worldly affairs, and his scholarly lineage. As you read, notice how the text uses both direct report and panegyric to convey his status.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the dual transmission chains that authenticate the biography.
The passage begins with a chain from al-Samarqandi to al-Shirazi, then another chain from al-Ghassani.
2
Identify the key figures
The passage mentions Abu Sa'd, his father Abu Bakr, his brother Abu Nasr, and the poet al-Sahib ibn 'Abbad. Understand their relationships.
Abu Sa'd took knowledge from his father Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili.
3
Analyze the praise
Al-Sahib's epistle uses vivid metaphors. Examine how he elevates Abu Sa'd as 'the scholar son of the scholar' and what that implies about his status.
The praise also highlights Abu Sa'd's teaching, ifta', lecturing, narration, writing, and dictation skills.
4
Consider the significance
Reflect on why Ibn 'Asakir includes this biography and what it teaches about scholarly ideals in Islamic history.
The biography shows the integration of religious and worldly leadership in medieval Islamic society.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أخبرنا الشيخ أبو القسم إسماعيل بن السمرقندى قال ثنا الشيخ الإمام أبو إسحق إبراهيم ابن علی بن یوسف الشيرازي قال أبو سعد إسماعيل بن أحمد بن إبراهيم بن إسماعيل بن العباس الإسماعيلي مات سنة ست وتسعين وثلاثمائة وجمع بين رياسة الدين والدنيا بجرجان وكان فقيهاً أديباً جواداً أخذ العلم عن أبيه أبي بكر الإسماعيلى وفيه وفى أخيه أبي نصر وأبيهما أبى بكر يقول الصاحب بن عباد في رسالته : وأما الفقيه أبو نصر فإذا جاء حدثنا وأخبرنا فصادع وصادق ونافذ وناطق وأما أنت أيها الفقيه أبا سعد فمن يراك كيف تدرس وتفتى وتحاضر وتروى وتكتب وتملى علم أنك الحبر بن الحبر والبحر ابن البحر والضياء بن الفجر وأبو سعد بن أبي بكر بن نجم الله شيخكم الأكبر فإن الثناء عليه غنم والنساء بمثله عقم فليفخر به أهل جرجان ما سال واديها وأذن مناديها
أخبرنا الشيخ أبو الحسن بن أبي العباس الغساني قال ثنا أحمد بن على البغدادي قال حدثني أبو سعد إسماعيل بن على بن الحسن الواعظ الأستراباذي قال توفى أبو سعد الإسماعيلي بجرجان في شهر ربيع الآخر من سنة ست وتسعين وثلاثمائة
The shaykh Abu al-Qasim Isma'il ibn al-Samarqandi informed us, saying: The imam Abu Ishaq Ibrahim ibn Ali ibn Yusuf al-Shirazi narrated to us, saying: Abu Sa'd Isma'il ibn Ahmad ibn Ibrahim ibn Isma'il ibn al-Abbas al-Isma'ili died in the year 396 AH. He combined the leadership of religion and the world in Jurjan. He was a jurist, a man of letters, generous. He took knowledge from his father Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili. Regarding him, his brother Abu Nasr, and their father Abu Bakr, al-Sahib ibn 'Abbad says in his epistle: 'As for the jurist Abu Nasr, when he comes and says 'haddathana' and 'akhbarana', he is a proclaimer, truthful, penetrating, and articulate. And as for you, O jurist Abu Sa'd, whoever sees you—how you teach, give legal opinions, lecture, narrate, write, and dictate—knows that you are the scholar son of the scholar, the sea son of the sea, the light son of the dawn. Abu Sa'd ibn Abi Bakr ibn Najm Allah, your greatest shaykh; indeed praise of him is gain, and women (giving birth) to someone like him are barren. So let the people of Jurjan take pride in him as long as its valley flows and its caller calls out.'
The shaykh Abu al-Hasan ibn Abi al-Abbas al-Ghassani informed us, saying: Ahmad ibn Ali al-Baghdadi narrated to us, saying: Abu Sa'd Isma'il ibn Ali ibn al-Hasan al-Wa'iz al-Astarabadi narrated to me, saying: Abu Sa'd al-Isma'ili died in Jurjan in the month of Rabi' al-Akhir of the year 396 AH.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry for Abu Sa'd al-Isma'ili, transmitted by two different chains. It opens with a chain from al-Samarqandi to al-Shirazi, who states that Abu Sa'd died in 396 AH and that he combined religious and worldly leadership in Jurjan. He is described as a jurist (faqih), a man of letters (adib), and generous (jawad). He studied under his father Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili. The passage then quotes a poetic praise from al-Sahib ibn 'Abbad, who extols both Abu Nasr (the brother) and Abu Sa'd (the subject), using vivid metaphors: Abu Sa'd is 'the scholar son of the scholar, the sea son of the sea, the light son of the dawn'. The praise emphasizes his teaching, ifta', lecturing, narration, writing, and dictation skills. Al-Sahib declares that praise of him is gain and that no one can match him. A second chain from al-Ghassani confirms the death date and place: Jurjan, in Rabi' al-Akhir 396 AH.

Key Terms
أبو سعد الإسماعيلي
الرياسة
الصاحب بن عباد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In what year did Abu Sa'd al-Isma'ili die according to this passage?
A) 396 AH
B) 397 AH
C) 386 AH
D) 406 AH

Key Takeaway
Abu Sa'd al-Isma'ili was a revered scholar-jurist of Jurjan who combined religious and worldly leadership and was celebrated in verse by al-Sahib ibn 'Abbad.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Abu Sa'd combined religious and worldly leadership. In which area of your life are you most neglecting your religious duties for worldly concerns? What specific change can you make today to rebalance them?
?
Al-Sahib ibn 'Abbad called Abu Sa'd 'the sea son of the sea' and 'the light son of the dawn.' What legacy are you building for those who will come after you? Will they see you as a source of light or of darkness?
?
You read that 'praise of him is gain, and women (giving birth) to someone like him are barren.' If you were to be described in similar terms, what would be said about your contribution to knowledge and generosity? How will you make yourself worthy of such praise?

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
beginner
5 min
The Noble Son of a Noble Father: Abu al-Tayyib al-Sa'luqi
Biographical entry with chains and anecdotes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key features of a classical biographical entry and appreciate the high scholarly status of Abu al-Tayyib al-Sa'luqi as described by Ibn Asakir.

Core Idea
A noble son of a noble father, Abu al-Tayyib combined religious and worldly leadership.

Ibn Asakir presents the biography of Abu al-Tayyib al-Sa'luqi, a prominent Hanafi jurist from Nisabur. Through chains of transmission and vivid anecdotes, the passage illustrates his scholarly excellence, his close relationship with his father, and the high regard in which he was held. Let us explore how this biography is structured and what it reveals.

Guided Path
1
Introduce the biographical subject
Read the full name and titles given to Abu al-Tayyib. Notice the emphasis on his lineage and his role as mufti of Nisabur.
The passage begins with a full chain of transmission to establish authority.
2
Identify the key anecdotes
Look for the stories about his father's praise, his handwriting, and the traveler's testimony. What do they convey about his character and scholarship?
These anecdotes serve as evidence of his excellence.
3
Reflect on the structure of a classical biography
Notice how Ibn Asakir uses multiple chains, lists of teachers and students, and personal accounts. This was the standard method of biographical writing.
The biography is not just facts; it is a witness to his virtue.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنهم أبو الطيب بن أبي سهل الصعلوکی النیسابوری رحمه الله كتب إلى الشيخ أبو نصر عبد الرحيم بن عبد الكريم بن هوازن قال أنا أبو بكر أحمد بن الحسين بن على الحافظ قال أنا أبو عبد الله محمد الله الحافظ قال : سهل بن محمد بن سلیمان بن محمد بن سلیمان بن عبد موسى ابن عيسى بن إبراهيم العجلى الفقيه الأديب أبو الطيب بن أبي سهل الخنفى الصعلوکی مفتی نيسابور وابن مفتيها وأكتب من رأينا من علمائنا وأنظرهم وقد كان بعض مشايخنا يقول من أراد أن يعلم أن النجيب بن النجيب يكون بمشيئة الله سبحانه وتعالى فلينظر إلى سهل ابن أبي سهل ، سمع أباه الأستاذ أبا سهل وعنده تفقه وبه تخرج وسمع أبا العباس محمد بن بن يعقوب وأبا على حامد بن محمد الهروي وأبا عمرو ابن نجيد السلمى وأقرانهم من الشيوخ ودرس الفقه واجتمع إليه الخلق اليوم الخامس من وفاة الأستاذ أبى سهل سنة تسع وستين وثلاثمائة وقد تخرج به جماعة من الفقهاء بنيسابور وسائر مدن خراسان وتصدروا للفتوى والقضاء والتدريس وخرجت الفوائد من سماعاته وحدث وأملى وبلغني أنه وضع في مجلسه أكثر من خمسمائة محبرة عشية الجمعة الثالث والعشرين من المحرم سنة سبع وثمانين وثلاثمائة . سمعت الأستاذ أبا سهل وذكر في مجلسه عقل ولده سهل وتمكينه منه وعلى همته وأكثروا وقالوا فلما فرغوا قال الأستاذ سهل والد ، ودخلت على الأستاذ رحمه الله في ابتداء مرضه وسهل غائب إلى بعض ضياعه فكان الأستاذ يشكو ما هو فيه فقال غيبة سهل أشد على من هذا الذي أنا فيه فلو حضر ما كنت أشكو مابي . هذا أو نحوه قال أبو عبد الله وسمعت الرئيس أبا محمد الميكالي غير مرة يقول الناس يعجبون من كتابة الأستاذ أبي سهل وسهل أكتب منه قال وسمعت أبا الأصبغ عبد العزيز بن عبد الملك وانصرف إلينا من نيسابوري ونحن ببخاری فسألناه ما الذى أستفدت هذه الكرة بنيسابور فقال رؤية سهل بن أبى سهل فإنى منذ فارقت وطنى بأقصى المغرب وجبت إلى أقصى المشرق ما رأيت مثله
أخبرنا الشيخ أبو القسم إسماعيل ابن أحمد بن السمرقندي قال ثنا الشيخ أبو إسحاق إبراهيم بن على الفيروزآبادي الفقيه قال : أبو الطيب سهل ابن محمد ابن سلیمان بن محمد بن سليمان الصعلوكي الحنفى من بنى حنيفة تفقه على أبيه أبي سهل وكان فقيهاً أديباً جمع رياسة الدين والدنيا وأخذ عنه فقهاء نيسابور
أخبرنا الشيخ أبو المعالي محمد بن إسماعيل بن محمد ابن الحسين الفارسى بنيسابور قال أنا الشيخ أبو بكر أحمد بن الحسين ابن على البيهقي قال أبو عبد الله الحافظ قال سمعت الشيخ أبا الوليد حسان بن محمد
And among them is Abu al-Tayyib ibn Abi Sahl al-Sa'luqi al-Nisaburi, may Allah have mercy on him. [A chain:] He wrote to the shaykh Abu Nasr Abd al-Rahim ibn Abd al-Karim ibn Hawazin, saying: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn al-Husayn ibn Ali al-Hafiz informed us, saying: Abu Abd Allah Muhammad Allah al-Hafiz informed us, saying: Sahl ibn Muhammad ibn Sulayman ibn Muhammad ibn Sulayman ibn Abd Musa ibn Isa ibn Ibrahim al-'Ijli, the jurist, the man of letters, Abu al-Tayyib ibn Abi Sahl al-Hanafi al-Sa'luqi, the mufti of Nisabur and the son of its mufti, and the most excellent and most far-seeing of our scholars whom we have seen. Some of our shaykhs used to say: Whoever wants to know that the noble son of the noble is by the will of Allah, may He be exalted, let him look at Sahl ibn Abi Sahl. He heard from his father, the master Abu Sahl, and under him he studied fiqh and graduated. He also heard from Abu al-Abbas Muhammad ibn Ya'qub, Abu Ali Hamid ibn Muhammad al-Harawi, Abu Amr ibn Najid al-Sulami, and their peers among the shaykhs. He taught fiqh, and people gathered around him on the fifth day after the death of the master Abu Sahl in the year 369 AH. A group of jurists graduated under him in Nisabur and all cities of Khurasan, and they became prominent in giving fatwas, judgment, and teaching. The benefits (of his narrations) were extracted from his hearings, and he narrated and dictated. It reached me that he placed more than five hundred inkwells in his study circle on the evening of Friday, the 23rd of Muharram in the year 387 AH. I heard the master Abu Sahl mention in his gathering the intelligence of his son Sahl, his mastery of it, his high aspiration, and they spoke at length. When they finished, the master Abu Sahl said: 'Sahl is (my) son.' And I entered upon the master, may Allah have mercy on him, at the beginning of his illness, and Sahl was absent in one of his estates. The master was complaining of his condition, so he said: 'The absence of Sahl is more severe upon me than what I am in. If he were present, I would not complain of what is wrong with me.' This or something similar. Abu Abd Allah said: I heard the chief Abu Muhammad al-Mikali more than once saying: 'People marvel at the handwriting of the master Abu Sahl, but Sahl writes better than him.' He said: And I heard Abu al-Asbagh Abd al-Aziz ibn Abd al-Malik—and he had come to us from Nisabur while we were in Bukhara—we asked him: 'What did you gain this time in Nisabur?' He said: 'The sight of Sahl ibn Abi Sahl, for since I left my homeland in the far Maghrib and journeyed to the far Mashriq, I have not seen the like of him.'
The shaykh Abu al-Qasim Isma'il ibn Ahmad ibn al-Samarqandi informed us, saying: The shaykh Abu Ishaq Ibrahim ibn Ali al-Firuzabadi al-Faqih narrated to us, saying: Abu al-Tayyib Sahl ibn Muhammad ibn Sulayman ibn Muhammad ibn Sulayman al-Sa'luqi al-Hanafi, from the tribe of Hanifa, studied fiqh under his father Abu Sahl. He was a jurist and man of letters; he combined the leadership of religion and the world, and the jurists of Nisabur took from him.
The shaykh Abu al-Ma'ali Muhammad ibn Isma'il ibn Muhammad ibn al-Husayn al-Farsi in Nisabur informed us, saying: The shaykh Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn al-Husayn ibn Ali al-Bayhaqi informed us, saying: Abu Abd Allah al-Hafiz said: I heard the shaykh Abu al-Walid Hassan ibn Muhammad...
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry for Abu al-Tayyib al-Sa'luqi, transmitted through multiple chains. It begins with a chain from al-Samarqandi and al-Shirazi, but the first part is an extended quote from an earlier authority (Abu Abd Allah al-Hafiz) who provides the full name and lineage of the subject: Sahl ibn Muhammad ibn Sulayman... al-'Ijli al-Hanafi al-Sa'luqi, the mufti of Nisabur and son of its mufti. He is described as the most excellent and far-seeing scholar. The passage then reports a saying from some shaykhs: to see a noble son of a noble, look at Sahl ibn Abi Sahl. It lists his teachers, primarily his father Abu Sahl, and other shaykhs like Muhammad ibn Ya'qub, Hamid al-Harawi, and Abu Amr al-Sulami. It notes that he taught fiqh and students gathered after his father's death in 369 AH. Many jurists of Nisabur and Khurasan studied under him and later became prominent. A remarkable detail: his study circle once had over five hundred inkwells on a Friday evening in 387 AH. There is a story about his father's illness: when Abu Sahl was sick and Sahl was absent, the father said Sahl's absence was worse than the illness itself. Another story from al-Mikali praises Sahl's handwriting as better than his father's. Finally, a traveler from the far Maghrib, Abu al-Asbagh, states that in all his journeys to the far Mashriq he never saw anyone like Sahl. The passage closes with two additional chains summarizing his name and that he combined religious and worldly leadership, and that jurists studied under him.

Key Terms
أبو الطيب الصعلوكي
سهل بن أبي سهل
مفتي نيسابور
رياسة الدين والدنيا

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What did the traveler Abu al-Asbagh say about Sahl ibn Abi Sahl when asked what he gained from his trip to Nisabur?
A) He gained many books
B) He saw Sahl and had never seen his like from Maghrib to Mashriq
C) He learned a new fiqh method
D) He collected many hadith

Key Takeaway
Abu al-Tayyib al-Sa'luqi was a distinguished Hanafi jurist who embodied the ideal of a noble son following in his father's footsteps, combining religious authority with worldly leadership.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You read how Abu al-Tayyib inherited excellence from his father and became a leader in both religion and world. What is one area of your life where you are not living up to the example of a righteous parent or teacher? What concrete step will you take this week to change that?
?
The narrator said he saw no one like Sahl in all his travels from west to east. If someone were to describe you after meeting you, would they say they have seen no one like you in terms of character and knowledge? What are you doing to become that kind of person?
?
When his father was ill, he said Sahl's absence was more severe than his illness. Do you have a relationship with a parent or teacher so strong that your absence would be felt so deeply? If not, what are you willing to sacrifice to build that bond?

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
beginner
5 min
The Esteemed Scholar Sahl ibn Abi Sahl
Ibn Asakir narrates the father's praise of Sahl's intelligence and his concern during illness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the extraordinary respect and admiration that Sahl ibn Abi Sahl commanded from his father and contemporaries, as recorded by Ibn Asakir.

Core Idea
Sahl ibn Abi Sahl was so esteemed that his father called him 'father' and others declared him unmatched.

This passage from Ibn Asakir's biography presents a vivid picture of the scholar Sahl ibn Abi Sahl, showcasing his education, his teaching career, and the high praise he received from those who knew him best, including his own father. As you read, notice how the narrative builds a portrait of a man whose intellectual and personal virtues set him apart.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Pay attention to the sequence: education, teaching, praise from father, and testimonies from others.
2
Identify the key testimonies
Note the father's statement 'Sahl is a father' and his complaint about Sahl's absence. Also note the praise from Abu Muhammad al-Mikali and Abu al-Asghagh about Sahl's handwriting and overall excellence.
These testimonies show the high regard Sahl held.
3
Reflect on the father's metaphor
The father calling his son 'father' is a striking metaphor. Think about what it suggests about Sahl's maturity and status.
It implies Sahl was a source of guidance and strength.
4
Consider the broader significance
This account is not just about Sahl; it illustrates the high standards of scholarship and character in that tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النجيب بن النجيب يكون بمشيئة الله سبحانه وتعالى فلينظر إلى سهل ابن أبي سهل ، سمع أباه الأستاذ أبا سهل وعنده تفقه وبه تخرج وسمع أبا العباس محمد بن بن يعقوب وأبا على حامد بن محمد الهروي وأبا عمرو ابن نجيد السلمى وأقرانهم من الشيوخ ودرس الفقه واجتمع إليه الخلق اليوم الخامس من وفاة الأستاذ أبى سهل سنة تسع وستين وثلاثمائة وقد تخرج به جماعة من الفقهاء بنيسابور وسائر مدن خراسان وتصدروا للفتوى والقضاء والتدريس وخرجت الفوائد من سماعاته وحدث وأملى وبلغني أنه وضع في مجلسه أكثر من خمسمائة محبرة عشية الجمعة الثالث والعشرين من المحرم سنة سبع وثمانين وثلاثمائة . سمعت الأستاذ أبا سهل وذكر في مجلسه عقل ولده سهل وتمكينه منه وعلى همته وأكثروا وقالوا فلما فرغوا قال الأستاذ سهل والد ، ودخلت على الأستاذ رحمه الله في ابتداء مرضه وسهل غائب إلى بعض ضياعه فكان الأستاذ يشكو ما هو فيه فقال غيبة سهل أشد على من هذا الذي أنا فيه فلو حضر ما كنت أشكو مابي . هذا أو نحوه قال أبو عبد الله وسمعت الرئيس أبا محمد الميكالي غير مرة يقول الناس يعجبون من كتابة الأستاذ أبي سهل وسهل أكتب منه قال وسمعت أبا الأصبغ عبد العزيز بن عبد الملك وانصرف إلينا من نيسابوري ونحن ببخاری فسألناه ما الذى أستفدت هذه الكرة بنيسابور فقال رؤية سهل بن أبى سهل فإنى منذ فارقت وطنى بأقصى المغرب وجبت إلى أقصى المشرق ما رأيت مثله
The noble son of a noble man, by the will of God the Exalted, so look to Sahl ibn Abi Sahl. He heard from his father the master Abu Sahl, and with him he studied jurisprudence (fiqh) and under him he graduated. He heard from Abu al-Abbas Muhammad ibn Ya'qub, Abu Ali Hamid ibn Muhammad al-Harawi, Abu Amr ibn Najid al-Sulami, and their peers among the shaykhs. He studied jurisprudence (fiqh), and people gathered to him on the fifth day after the death of the master Abu Sahl in the year 369 AH. A group of jurists (fuqaha) graduated under him in Nishapur and other cities of Khurasan, and they became heads in issuing legal opinions (fatwa), judgeship (qada), and teaching (tadris). Benefits (fawa'id) came out from his hearings, and he narrated (hadith) and dictated. It reached me that in his study circle more than five hundred inkstands were placed on the evening of Friday, the twenty-third of Muharram in the year 387 AH. I heard the master Abu Sahl mention in his study circle the intellect of his son Sahl, his mastery of him, and his high aspiration, and they spoke much. When they finished, the master said: 'Sahl is a father.' I entered upon the master (may God have mercy on him) at the beginning of his illness while Sahl was absent at one of his estates. The master was complaining of what he was in, so he said: 'The absence of Sahl is harder on me than what I am in. If he were present, I would not complain of what is with me.' This or similar. Abu Abdullah said: I heard the chief Abu Muhammad al-Mikali more than once saying: 'People marvel at the handwriting of the master Abu Sahl, but Sahl writes better than him.' He said: I heard Abu al-Asbagh Abd al-Aziz ibn Abd al-Malik—and he had returned to us from Nishapur while we were in Bukhara—so we asked him: 'What did you gain this time in Nishapur?' He said: 'Seeing Sahl ibn Abi Sahl. For since I left my homeland in the far Maghrib and traveled to the far Mashriq, I have not seen the like of him.'
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account of Sahl ibn Abi Sahl (also known as Sahl ibn Muhammad al-Sa'luqi), compiled by Ibn Asakir. The narrative begins by describing him as a noble son of a noble man, then details his education: he studied under his father Abu Sahl, who was a master shaykh, and also heard from several other prominent shaykhs of the time. After his father's death in 369 AH, Sahl took up teaching, and a large number of students gathered around him on the fifth day following the death. He taught jurisprudence (fiqh) and produced many jurists who later became leaders in legal opinions, judgeship, and teaching across Nishapur and other cities of Khurasan. The passage then records a remarkable testimony from his father: during a gathering, after others praised Sahl's intellect, mastery, and high aspiration, Abu Sahl said 'Sahl is a father'—a phrase indicating that his son was like a father to him, perhaps because of his maturity. When Abu Sahl fell ill and Sahl was away, the master complained that Sahl's absence was harder on him than the illness itself. Then Abu Abdullah reports that Chief Abu Muhammad al-Mikali testified that Sahl's handwriting was even better than his father's. Finally, Abu al-Asbagh, a traveler from the far Maghrib, stated that after traveling to the farthest East, he had seen no one like Sahl. This lesson presents the extraordinary esteem in which Sahl was held by his father and contemporaries.

Key Terms
سهل ابن أبي سهل
الأستاذ أبو سهل
تفقه
الفتوى
القضاء
التدريس
المحبرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The father's statement 'سهل والد' might be taken literally, as if Sahl was physically his father.
Correction: It is a metaphor for Sahl's high status and maturity, indicating that Sahl was like a father figure due to his wisdom and guidance.

Checkpoint

A) 'I am content with his absence.'
B) 'His absence is harder on me than this illness.'
C) 'Send for him immediately.'
D) 'I do not need him.'

Key Takeaway
Sahl ibn Abi Sahl was so revered that his father considered his absence worse than illness, and travelers deemed him unmatched across the Islamic world.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
When you are away from those who depend on you—your family, your teachers, your community—does your absence cause them pain or relief? Reflect on whether your presence is a source of strength like Sahl's, or merely a convenience.
?
The traveler from the far Maghrib declared he had seen no one like Sahl after journeying across the Islamic world. If someone traveled from your city to the ends of the earth, would they find anyone who speaks of you with such unmatched reverence? What legacy are you building right now, in your daily interactions?

A separate chain of transmission testifies to Sahl's learning and leadership.

Learning Objective

Core Idea
A second isnad confirms Sahl's unique combination of religious and worldly leadership.

This lesson presents a second chain of transmission that attests to the excellence of Sahl al-Sa'luqi. The passage, narrated by al-Samarqandi from al-Firuzabadi, emphasizes that Sahl was not only a jurist but also combined leadership in both religious and worldly matters. It serves as independent testimony to his scholarly and social stature.

A Poem in Praise of Imam al-Sa'luqi
A final poetic eulogy for Sahl, comparing him to a pearl and a guiding light.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the poetic tribute paid to Imam al-Sa'luqi by his contemporary, highlighting his esteemed status as a hidden gem among scholars.

Core Idea
The pearl hidden in the shell: true worth is often concealed.

This lesson presents a short poem composed by Abu al-Nadr al-Utbi and sent to Imam al-Sa'luqi. The poem uses beautiful imagery to express deep respect for the scholar, comparing him to a precious pearl and a guiding light. As you read, notice how the poet elevates Sahl's status while acknowledging his humility.

Guided Path
1
Read the poem and translation

The poem is short but dense in metaphor.

Identify the key images

3
Reflect on the pearl metaphor
The poet says 'you are its sash' (an ornament) and then 'the pearl is in the oyster shell.' This suggests something valuable but hidden. Why would a poet emphasize hidden worth?
Consider the humility of scholars.
4
Understand the context
This poem was written by a contemporary and sent directly to Imam al-Sa'luqi. Think about what it reveals about the community's view of him.

It then compares Sahl to a valuable pearl inside an oyster shell, implying that his worth is hidden but precious. The poem is a conventional but elegant tribute, reinforcing the high esteem in which Sahl was held by his contemporaries.

The Prediction of the Third Renewer
Ibn Asakir narrates the prediction that the qadi is the third renewer of the century.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Islamic tradition of tajdid (renewal) was applied to specific scholars through this anecdote about the judge Abu al-Abbas.

Core Idea
Being named a renewer can be a grave announcement, not just an honor.

This passage is a vivid historical account that brings the concept of tajdid to life. It narrates a prediction made to the judge Abu al-Abbas, declaring him the renewer of the third Islamic century. As you read, notice the mix of glad tidings and solemn foreboding, and how the judge himself interprets the prediction as a notice of his death.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Pay attention to the flow of the story: the setting, the scholar's speech, the poem, and the reaction.
The Arabic may have minor OCR errors; trust the translation.
2
Identify the three renewers mentioned
The scholar lists three renewers. Note who they are and the centuries they represent. Understand the historical context of each figure.
Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz (first), al-Shafi'i (second), and the judge (third).
3
Reflect on the judge's reaction
Why did the judge weep and say 'he has announced my death to me'? Think about the emotional weight of being named a mujaddid and the tradition that renewers often die soon after their century begins.
The judge died the same year, according to the narrator.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفقيه يقول كنا في مجلس القاضي أبي العباس بن سنة ثلاث وثلاثمائة فقام إليه شيخ من أهل العلم فقال أبشر أيها القاضي فإن الله يبعث على رأس كل مائة سنة يعني من يحدد لها يعني للأمة أمر دينها وأنه تعالى بعث على رأس المائة عمر بن عبد العزيز وتوفي سنة يعني إحدى ومائة وبعث على رأس المأتين أبا عبد الله محمد بن إدريس الشافعي وتوفى سنة أربع وثمانين وبعثك على رأس الثلاثمائة ثم أنشأ يقول : اثنان قد مضيا فبورك فيهما عمر الخليفة ثم حلف السؤدد الشافعي الألمعي محمد أرث النبوة وابن عم محمد . أبشر أبا العباس أنك ثالث من بعدهم سقيا لتربة أحمد قال فصاح أبو العباس القاضي وبكى فقال قد نعى إلى نفسى قال الشيخ أبو الوليد فمات القاضي أبو العباس في تلك السنة
The jurist says: We were in the gathering of the judge Abu al-Abbas ibn Sanah in the year three hundred and three. Then an elderly scholar stood up to him and said: 'Rejoice, O judge, for Allah sends at the head of every hundred years one who renews for the community the matters of its religion. And He sent at the head of the first hundred Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz, and he died in the year one hundred and one. And He sent at the head of the two hundred Abu Abd Allah Muhammad ibn Idris al-Shafi'i, and he died in the year one hundred and eighty-four. And He has sent you at the head of the three hundred.' Then he composed saying: 'Two have passed, blessed are they: Umar the Caliph, then the lord of majesty, al-Shafi'i the astute Muhammad, heir to prophethood and cousin of Muhammad. Rejoice, Abu al-Abbas, you are third after them; may the soil of Ahmad be watered.' He said: So the judge Abu al-Abbas cried out and wept, and said: 'He has announced my death to me.' Al-Shaykh Abu al-Walid said: So the judge Abu al-Abbas died in that year.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage is a biographical anecdote recounting a prediction about the judge Abu al-Abbas. It begins with the jurist narrating that they were in the judge's gathering in the year 303 AH. An elderly scholar stood up and gave him glad tidings, citing the well-known tradition that Allah sends a renewer (mujaddid) at the beginning of every century. The scholar enumerates the known renewers: Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz for the first century (who died in 101 AH), al-Shafi'i for the second (died in 204 AH, noted erroneously as 184 AH in the text), and then declares that the judge himself is the renewer for the third century. He then recites a poem praising the two predecessors and declaring the judge the third. The judge's reaction is one of sorrow and weeping; he interprets the prediction as a notification of his impending death. The narrator, Abu al-Walid, confirms that the judge died that same year. The passage illustrates how the concept of tajdid (renewal) was applied to specific scholars and the dramatic response it could evoke.

Key Terms
محدث
مجدد
القاضي أبو العباس
عمر بن عبد العزيز
الشافعي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The passage is claiming that the judge was infallible or that the prediction was a divine decree.
Correction: The passage does not assert infallibility; it simply reports a scholar's application of the tajdid tradition and the judge's own interpretation of it as a death notice.

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The judge wept when told he was a renewer because he understood the gravity. When was the last time you wept over a blessing from Allah, realizing it might be a test or a farewell? What keeps you from feeling that way now?
?

Sahl al-Sa'luki: Renewer and Scholar's Dream
Three anecdotes highlighting Sahl al-Sa'luki's status as a renewer and the afterlife merit of knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sahl al-Sa'luki was recognized as a renewer of the faith and the significance of his dream regarding the afterlife benefit of scholarly questions.

Core Idea
Poetry and dreams testify to a scholar's rank and the eternal reward of knowledge.

This passage from Ibn 'Asakir's Tabayin combines two powerful testimonies to the stature of Imam Sahl al-Sa'luki: a poetic enumeration placing him among the renewers of Islam, and a dream in which he reveals that his scholarly efforts earned him divine forgiveness. Together, they illustrate how the tradition of tajdid (renewal) was celebrated in biographical literature and how knowledge was believed to benefit its possessor even in the afterlife.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage moves from historical report to poetry to dream.
2
Identify the renewal claim
The poem names Sahl as the fourth renewer. Notice how al-Hakim reacts and the significance of the timing (at the head of four hundred years).
This continues the tajdid tradition from earlier in the text.
3
Examine the symbolic poem
Al-Utbi's poem uses metaphor (pearl, scabbard) to describe hidden greatness. Understand the imagery and why it fits Sahl.
The pearl guarded by its shell reflects the scholar's inner worth.
4
Analyze the dream account
Read the dream: Sahl dismisses his spiritual states but is forgiven for 'questions about which helplessness was asked'. Grasp that this points to the value of answering difficult scholarly problems.
The phrase 'questions about which helplessness was asked' indicates challenging scholarly inquiries.
5
Reflect on the lesson
Consider what this passage teaches about the role of knowledge and the honor of scholars in Islamic tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الحاكم أبو عبد الله فلما رويت هذه الحكاية كتبوها وكان ممن كتبها شيخ أديب فقيه فلما كان فى المجلس الثانى قال لى بعض الحاضرين أن هذا الشيخ قد زاد في تلك الأبيات ذكر الشيخ أبي الطيب سهل بن محمد وجعله على رأس الأربعمائة فسألت ذلك الفقيه عنه فأنشدني قوله فى قصيدة مدحه بها : والرابع المشهور سهل محمد أضحى إماما عند كل موحد يأوى إليه المسلمون بأسرهم فى العلم أن جاءوا بخطب مريد لا زال فيما بيننا شيخ الورى للمذهب المختار خير مجدد قال الحاكم فسكت ولم أنطق وغمنى ذلك إلى أن قدر الله وفاته رحمه الله في تلك السنة. أنشدنا الشيخ أبو حفص عمر بن على بن أحمد الطوسي ثم النوقاني الفقيه المعروف بالفاضلي البخترى بنوقان قال أنشدنا الشيخ الرئيس أبو إبراهيم أسعد بن مسعود العتبى أملاء بنيسابور قال أنشدني جدى الشيخ أبو النضر يعنى العتبى النيسابورى لنفسه فيما كتب إلى الإمام الصعلوكي : ألا أيها الشيخ الإمام ومن به تبلج فجر الدهر عن فلق البشر لكن كنت فى الدنيا وأنت وشاحها عيانا فإن الدر في صدف البحر. ولم تحوك الدنيا لأنك دونها ولكن لب الشئ يحرز بالقشر وقد صين نصل السيف تحت قرابه كما صين نور العين في الجفن والشعر. سمعت أبا المظفر بن أبى القسم القشيرى يقول سمعت أبي يقول سمعت أبا سعيد الشحام يقول رأيت الشيخ الإمام أبا الطيب سهل الصعلوكي في المنام فقلت أيها الشيخ فقال دع الشيخ فقلت وتلك الأحوال التي شاهدتها فقال لم تغن عنا فقلت ما فعل الله بك فقال غفر لى بمسائل كانت تسل عنها العجز.
Al-Hakim Abu Abd Allah said: When I narrated this story, they wrote it down, and among those who wrote it was a learned and cultured jurist. Then at the second gathering, one of those present said to me: 'This shaykh has added in those verses a mention of Shaykh Abu al-Tayyib Sahl ibn Muhammad and placed him at the head of four hundred.' So I asked that jurist about him, and he recited to me his saying in a poem praising him: 'And the fourth, the famous Sahl Muhammad, has become an imam for every monotheist. Muslims all take refuge in him, in knowledge, when they come with a serious matter. He remains among us, the shaykh of mankind, for the chosen madhhab, the best renewer.' Al-Hakim said: I kept silent and did not speak, and it distressed me until Allah decreed his death, may Allah have mercy on him, in that year. We were recited by Shaykh Abu Hafs Umar ibn Ali ibn Ahmad al-Tusi then al-Nuqani, the jurist known as al-Fadili al-Bukhtari, in Nuqan, who said: We were recited by the chief shaykh Abu Ibrahim As'ad ibn Mas'ud al-Utbi, in dictation in Nishapur, who said: My grandfather, Shaykh Abu al-Nadr, meaning al-Utbi al-Nisaburi, recited to me of his own composition in a letter to Imam al-Sa'luki: 'Behold, O shaykh and imam, by whom the dawn of time has shone from the cleft of mankind! But you were in the world as its sash, visible, for the pearl is in the shell of the sea. And the world did not weave you because you are above it; rather the core of a thing is guarded by the shell. And the sword blade is preserved under its scabbard, as the light of the eye is preserved in eyelid and hair.' I heard Abu al-Muzaffar ibn Abi al-Qasim al-Qushayri say: I heard my father say: I heard Abu Sa'id al-Shahham say: I saw Shaykh Imam Abu al-Tayyib Sahl al-Sa'luki in a dream, and I said: 'O shaykh!' He said: 'Leave the shaykh.' I said: 'And those states that you witnessed?' He said: 'They did not avail us.' I said: 'What did Allah do with you?' He said: 'He forgave me because of questions about which helplessness was asked.'
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage continues the theme of tajdid (renewal) and then includes a dream account. It begins with al-Hakim Abu Abd Allah narrating that the story of the qadi's prediction was written down. Later, in another gathering, someone told him that a shaykh had added verses mentioning Sahl ibn Muhammad as the fourth renewer at the head of four hundred years. Al-Hakim asked the jurist and received a poem in praise of Sahl, calling him the fourth famous renewer, an imam for monotheists. Al-Hakim remained silent but was distressed; later Sahl died that same year. Then a separate chain of narration brings a poem by al-Utbi to Imam al-Sa'luki, using imagery of the pearl in the shell and the sword in its scabbard to describe the imam's hidden greatness. Finally, a dream is related: al-Sa'luki appears to Abu Sa'id al-Shahham. When asked about his spiritual states, he dismisses them as not beneficial, but says he was forgiven because of the questions (masa'il) about which helplessness was expressed — likely referring to difficult scholarly questions he had answered. The passage shows the high regard for Sahl al-Sa'luki as a renewer and the belief in the afterlife benefit of knowledge.

Key Terms
مجدد
سهل بن محمد
الصعلوكي
مسائل
المنام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The dream of Sahl al-Sa'luki is a source of theological rulings about the afterlife.
Correction: The dream is a personal vision reported to illustrate the virtue of knowledge, not a source of doctrine.

Checkpoint
What did al-Sa'luki say he was forgiven for in the dream?
A) His asceticism
B) His prayers
C) Questions about which helplessness was asked
D) His poems

Key Takeaway
The legacy of a scholar is celebrated through poetry and even in dreams, affirming that sincere scholarship leads to divine mercy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you accumulate Islamic knowledge, do you hoard it like a pearl in a shell, or do you let it shine for others? What is one difficult question someone has asked you that you avoided? Will you answer it now for Allah's sake?
?
Sahl's spiritual states did not avail him, yet he was forgiven for answering tough questions. What are you relying on for your salvation? Is it your worship or your service to others' understanding? How can you shift your focus today?
?
Al-Hakim was distressed by the praise given to Sahl. When others praise you, do you feel discomfort or pride? Can you name a time your ego inflated from praise, and how can you train yourself to deflect credit to Allah?

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir

The Biography of Abu al-Hasan ibn Dawud al-Darani
Ibn Asakir records the death, teachers, Ash'ari affiliation, and story of Ibn Dawud.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ibn Asakir's biographical entry presents Abu al-Hasan ibn Dawud as a model of piety, scholarship, and Ash'ari affiliation.

Core Idea
A humble imam from Dariya became the leader of Damascus — because of his knowledge and piety.

Ibn Asakir's biographical entry on Abu al-Hasan ibn Dawud al-Muqri al-Darani is more than a record of dates and names. It reveals how a scholar's reputation could transcend his locality, and how Ash'ari affiliation was noted as a marker of orthodoxy. The story of his being called to lead the entire Damascus mosque underscores his esteemed position. This lesson unpacks the layers of this short but rich entry.

Guided Path
1
Read the biographical data
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Note the chain of transmission, death date, and scholarly credentials.
Observe how Ibn Asakir uses multiple sources to establish reliability.
2
Identify the Ash'ari affiliation
Find the explicit statement that Ibn Dawud followed the madhhab of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari. Understand that this was recorded as a point of merit.
This shows Ash'ari theology as a recognized school within Sunni Islam.
3
Analyze the story of his appointment
Read the anecdote about the people of Dariya arming themselves to keep him, and the resolution by Abu Muhammad ibn Abi Nasr.
Consider what this story reveals about the community's love for their imam.
4
Reflect on the humility demonstrated
Notice that Ibn Dawud refused the judge's mule and rode his own donkey. This shows his humility despite his high rank.
Humility is a recurring theme in Sunni biographical literature.

And among them is Abu al-Hasan ibn Dawud al-Muqri al-Darani al-Dimashqi, may Allah have mercy on him. The trustworthy Abu Muhammad Hibat Allah ibn Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn al-Akfani informed us, saying: Abu Muhammad Abd al-Aziz ibn Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Ali al-Tamimi al-Sufi al-Katani narrated to us, saying: I heard a group of our shaykhs say: Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Dawud al-Muqri al-Darani died on Wednesday after asr, on the sixth day of Jumada al-Ula of the year four hundred and two. Among those who went out with them was the judge Abu Abd Allah ibn al-Nasiy al-Husayni and the prominent shaykhs of the city, such as Abu Muhammad ibn Abi Nasr and others. Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry for Abu al-Hasan ibn Dawud al-Muqri al-Darani. It begins with the chain of transmission: al-Akfani from al-Katani from a group of shaykhs. They report his death date: Wednesday after asr, 6 Jumada al-Ula 402 AH. Abd al-Aziz notes that Ibn Dawud recited to Ibn al-Akhram and became the leader in qira'a (Quranic recitation) for the Syrians. He narrated from several teachers. His funeral was attended, and he was described as trustworthy, reliable, and righteous. Importantly, it states that he followed the madhhab of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari. He used to lead prayer in the Damascus mosque. The passage then narrates a famous story: Ibn Dawud was the imam of the people of Dariya (a suburb). When the imam of the main Damascus mosque died, the Damascenes went to Dariya to bring Ibn Dawud to be their imam. They sent a delegation including the judge and other shaykhs. The people of Dariya armed themselves, unwilling to lose their imam. Abu Muhammad ibn Abi Nasr convinced them: they should be proud that Damascus needed their imam. So they relented. Ibn Dawud refused the judge's mule and rode his own donkey, showing humility. The story cuts off at the page break, but the lesson contains the complete anecdote as far as the text provides. This story illustrates the high esteem in which Ibn Dawud was held and his adherence to Ash'ari theology.

?

?
The people of Dariya were ready to fight to keep their imam. Is there anyone in your life for whom you would sacrifice safety or convenience—and more importantly, are you someone others would sacrifice for? If not, what specific step will you take this week to become a person worth keeping?
?
When Ibn Dawud was taken to lead all of Damascus, he did not change his simple ways. If you were suddenly given a position of influence or authority tomorrow, what core habit or act of worship would you refuse to alter, no matter what others expected of you? Write it down now and commit to it.

Poetic Fragment and Dream of Sahl al-Sa'luqi
Poetic quote and dream narrative about Sahl al-Sa'luqi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the dream narrative of Sahl al-Sa'luqi and the lesson that sincere scholarly inquiry can be a means of salvation, even when spiritual states prove insufficient.

Core Idea
Scholarly questions outlast spiritual states in the afterlife.

This passage pairs a poetic metaphor about preserving virtue with a striking dream narrative. In the dream, the great Shafi'i jurist and Ash'ari theologian Sahl al-Sa'luqi reveals that his spiritual experiences did not help him in the grave, but his scholarly questions and efforts in theological inquiry earned God's forgiveness. This story underscores the enduring value of intellectual pursuit in Islam.

Guided Path
1
Read the poetic fragment
Read the Arabic poetry and its translation. Notice the imagery of preservation: the sword blade in its scabbard and the eye's light in the eyelid. Though the exact meaning of one word is unclear, the theme is about concealing and preserving something precious.
The unclear word 'بالقــــــــــر' may affect the precise metaphor, but the general idea is clear.
2
Read the dream narrative
Read the dream account with its chain of transmission. Identify the dreamer, the deceased scholar, and the key exchange. Notice that the shaykh dismisses his spiritual states and attributes his forgiveness to his scholarly questions.
The phrase 'تسل عنها العجز' suggests the questions were about matters that expose human incapacity, likely theological puzzles.
3
Reflect on the lesson
Consider why the shaykh's states were of no avail while his questions were beneficial. This teaches that sincere intellectual struggle in seeking truth can be a cause of divine mercy, even if one's mystical achievements are limited.
This aligns with the Ash'ari emphasis on sound theology and knowledge.
4
Apply to your own study
Think about how this dream encourages students of knowledge to value their studies and questions. Even if you do not reach high spiritual states, your sincere pursuit of knowledge can be a means of salvation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم تحوك الدنيا لأنك دونها ولكن لب الشئ يحرز بالقــــــــــر وقد صين نصل السيف تحت قرابه كما صين نور العين في الجفن والشعر سمعت أبا المظفر بن أبى القسم القشيرى يقول سمعت أبي يقول سمعت أبا سعيد الشحام يقول رأيت الشيخ الإمام أبا الطيب سهل الصعلوكي في المنام فقلت أيها الشيخ فقال دع الشيخ فقلت وتلك الأحوال التي شاهدتها فقال لم تغن عنا فقلت ما فعل الله بك فقال غفر لى بمسائل كانت تسل عنها العجز .
And the world did not weave you because you are beneath it, but the core of the thing is preserved in [؟]. And the sword's blade has been kept under its scabbard, as the light of the eye is kept in the eyelid and the hair. I heard Abu al-Muzaffar ibn Abi al-Qasim al-Qushayri say: I heard my father say: I heard Abu Sa'id al-Shahham say: I saw the Shaykh al-Imam Abu al-Tayyib Sahl al-Sa'luqi in a dream, and I said, 'O Shaykh!' He said, 'Leave the shaykh.' I said, 'And those states which you witnessed?' He said, 'They did not avail us.' I said, 'What did God do with you?' He said, 'He forgave me for [the sake of] questions about which incapacity would be asked.'
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage begins with a poetic fragment that seems metaphorical, comparing the preservation of a sword's blade in its scabbard to the preservation of the eye's light in the eyelid and hair. The meaning is unclear without context, but it likely extols the concealment of virtue. It is followed by a dream narrative with a chain of transmission: the author heard from Abu al-Muzaffar al-Qushayri, who heard from his father, who heard from Abu Sa'id al-Shahham, who recounts seeing the renowned Shafi'i jurist and Ash'ari theologian Sahl al-Sa'luqi (d. 404/1013) in a dream. In the dream, the dreamer asks about the states (ahwal) the deceased had experienced in his spiritual life. The shaykh dismisses the question, indicating that those states were of no benefit after death. When asked what God did with him, the shaykh replies that He forgave him because of (or for the sake of) questions (masa'il) about which incapacity (al-'ajz) would be asked. This suggests that his scholarly discussions and theological inquiries, which might have been a source of confusion or humility, were the means of his salvation. The lesson underscores the value of intellectual endeavor in the afterlife.

أبو الطيب سهل الصعلوكي
مسائل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the dream dismisses the value of spiritual states (ahwal) entirely and that only scholarly knowledge matters.
Correction: The dream does not deny the value of spiritual states in general, but it indicates that after death, it is sincere intellectual engagement – specifically the asking and wrestling of theological questions – that earned forgiveness for al-Sa'luqi. This highlights the importance of 'ilm (knowledge) but does not negate the worth of spiritual struggle.

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The dreamer called al-Sa'luqi 'Shaykh' and was rebuked. Are there titles or reputations you cherish that will crumble in the grave? Are you willing to let go of your need for recognition and instead focus on the knowledge that humbles you?
?
Al-Sa'luqi said his spiritual states did not avail him. What are you relying on—your efforts, your experiences, or your knowledge of your own weakness? If you stood before Allah right now, what would you hope He overlooks? How does this lesson change your prayer tonight?

Life of Imam Ibn Asakir
